-> Self {\n359:         Self { local_waker, ..self }\n360:     }\n361: \n362:     /// Sets the value for the extension data on `Context`.\n363:     #[inline]\n364:     #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n365:     pub const fn ext(self, data: &'a mut dyn Any) -> Self {\n366:         Self { ext: ExtData::Some(data), ..self }\n367:     }\n368: \n369:     /// Builds the `Context`.\n370:     #[inline]\n371:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n372:     pub const fn build(self) -> Context<'a> {\n373:         let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\n374:         Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\n375:     }\n376: }\n377: \n378: /// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\n379: /// is ready to be run.\n380: ///\n381: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n382: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n383: ///\n384: /// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n385: /// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n386: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\n387: /// the future should be polled again.\n388: ///\n389: /// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\n390: /// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\n391: /// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\n392: /// thread.\n393: ///\n394: /// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n395: /// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n396: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n397: ///\n398: /// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\n399: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n400: ///\n401: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n402: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n403: /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n404: #[repr(transparent)]\n405: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n406: #[rustc_diagnostic_item = \"Waker\"]\n407: pub struct Waker {\n408:     waker: RawWaker,\n409: }\n410: \n411: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n412: impl Unpin for Waker {}\n413: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n414: unsafe impl Send for Waker {}\n415: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n416: unsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\n417: \n418: impl Waker {\n419:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\n420:     ///\n421:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n422:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n423:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n424:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\n425:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n426:     /// unbounded processing loops.\n427:     ///\n428:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n429:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n430:     ///\n431:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n432:     /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n433:     /// current task again.\n434:     ///\n435:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n436:     #[inline]\n437:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n438:     pub fn wake(self) {\n439:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n440:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n441: \n442:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n443:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n444: \n445:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n446:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n447:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n448:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n449:     }\n450: \n451:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\n452:     ///\n453:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n454:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\n455:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\n456:     #[inline]\n457:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n458:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\n459:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n460:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n461: \n462:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\n463:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\n464:     }\n465: \n466:     /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\n467:     ///\n468:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\n469:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\n470:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n471:     ///\n472:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\n473:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n474:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n475:     #[inline]\n476:     #[must_use]\n477:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n478:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\n479:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n480:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n481:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n482:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n483:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n484:     }\n485: \n486:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n487:     ///\n488:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n489:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n490:     /// that is associated with the task.\n491:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n492:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n493:     ///\n494:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n495:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\n496:     ///\n497:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\n498:     /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\n499:     ///\n500:     /// # Safety\n501:     ///\n502:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n503:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n504:     ///\n505:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n506:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n507:     ///\n508:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n509:     #[inline]\n510:     #[must_use]\n511:     #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n512:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n513:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n514:         Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n515:     }\n516: \n517:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\n518:     ///\n519:     /// # Safety\n520:     ///\n521:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n522:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n523:     ///\n524:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n525:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n526:     ///\n527:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n528:     #[inline]\n529:     #[must_use]\n530:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n531:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n532:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\n533:         Waker { waker }\n534:     }\n535: \n536:     /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\n537:     ///\n538:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n539:     // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\n540:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n541:     //\n542:     /// again.\n548:     /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\n549:     ///\n550:     /// If an owned `Waker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\n551:     ///\n552:     /// # Examples\n553:     ///\n554:     /// ```\n555:     /// use std::future::Future;\n556:     /// use std::task;\n557:     ///\n558:     /// let mut cx = task::Poll::Ready(10));\n562:     /// ```\n563:     #[inline]\n564:     #[must_use]\n565:     #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n566:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n567:     pub const fn noop() -> &'static Waker {\n568:         const WAKER: &Waker = &Waker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\n569:         WAKER\n570:     }\n571: \n572:     /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n573:     #[inline]\n574:     #[must_use]\n575:     #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n576:     pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\n577:         self.waker.data\n578:     }\n579: \n580:     /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n581:     #[inline]\n582:     #[must_use]\n583:    }\n609: }\n610: \n611: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n612: impl Clone for Waker {\n613:     #[inline]\n614:     fn clone(&self) -> Self {\n615:         Waker {\n616: of [`RawWaker`] is upheld.\n619:             waker: unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.clone)(self.waker.data) },\n620:         }\n621:     }\n622: \n623:     /// Assigns a clone of `source` to `self`, unless [`self.will_wake(source)`][Waker::will_wake] anyway.\n624:     ///\n625:     /// This method is preferred over simply assigning `source.clone()` to `self`,\n626:     /// as it avoids cloning the waker if `self` is already the same waker.\n627:     ///\n628:     /// # Examples\n629:     ///\n630:     /// ```\n631:     /// use std::future::Future;\n632:     /// use std::pin::Pin;\n633:     /// use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\n634:     /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Waker};\n635:     ///\n636:     /// struct Waiter {\n637:     ///     shared: Arc<Mutex<Shared>>,\n638:     /// }\n639: ();\n647:     ///     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<()> {\n648:     ///         let mut shared = self.shared.lock().unwrap();\n649:     ///\n650:     ///         // update the waker\n651:     ///         shared.waker.clone_from(cx.waker());\n652:     ///\n653:     ///         // readiness logic ...\n654:     /// #       Poll::Ready(())\n655:     ///     }\n656:     /// }\n657:     ///\n658:     /// ```\n659:     #[inline]\n660:     fn clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\n661:         if !self.will_wake(source) {\n662:             *self = source.clone();\n663:         }\n664:     }\n665: }\n666: \n667: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n668: impl Drop for Waker {\n669:     #[inline]\n670:     fn drop(&mut self) of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n674:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.drop)(self.waker.data) }\n675:     }\n676: }\n677: \n678: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n679: impl fmt::Debug for Waker {\n680:     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n681:         let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\n682:         f.debug_struct(\"Waker\")\n683:             .field(\"data\", &self.waker.data)\n684:             .field(\"vtable\", &vtable_ptr)\n685:             .finish()\n686:     }\n687: }\n688: \n689: /// A `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\n690: ///\n691: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n692: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n693: ///\n694: /// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\n695: ///\n696: /// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n697: /// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n698: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\n699: /// the future should be polled again.\n700: ///\n701: /// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\n702: /// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\n703: /// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\n704: /// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\n705: ///\n706: /// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n707: /// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n708: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n709: ///\n710: /// # Examples\n711: /// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\n712: /// ```\n713: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\n714: /// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\n715: /// use std::task::Poll;\n716: ///\n717: /// // a future that returns pending once.\n718: /// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\n719: ///     let mut yielded = false;\n720: ///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\n721: ///         if !yielded {\n722: ///             yielded = true;\n723: ///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\n724: ///             return Poll::Pending;\n725: ///         }\n726: ///         return Poll::Ready(())\n727: ///     })\n728: /// }\n729: ///\n730: /// # async fn __() {\n731: /// yield_now().await;\n732: /// # }\n733: /// ```\n734: ///\n735: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n736: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n737: /// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\n738: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n739: #[repr(transparent)]\n740: pub struct LocalWaker {\n741:     waker: RawWaker,\n742: }\n743: \n744: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n745: impl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\n746: \n747: impl LocalWaker {\n748:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\n749:     ///\n750:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n751:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n752:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n753:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This makes\n754:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n755:     /// unbounded processing loops.\n756:     ///\n757:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n758:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n759:     ///\n760:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n761:     /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n762:     /// current task again.\n763:     ///\n764:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n765:     #[inline]\n766:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n767:     pub fn wake(self) {\n768:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n769:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n770: \n771:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n772:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n773: \n774:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n775:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n776:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n777:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n778:     }\n779: \n780:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker` without consuming the `LocalWaker`.\n781:     ///\n782:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n783:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. However, if this function\n799:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n800:     ///\n801:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\n802:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n803:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n804:     #[inline]\n805:     #[must_use]\n806:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n807:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &LocalWaker) -> bool {\n808:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n809:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n810:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n811:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n812:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n813:     }\n814: \n815:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n816:     ///\n817:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n818:     /// by the executor. Returning quickly prevents unnecessarily clogging up\\n93:     /// threads or event loops. If it is known ahead of time that a call to\\n94:     /// `poll` may end up taking a while, the work should be offloaded to a\\n95:     /// thread pool (or something similar) to ensure that `poll` can return\\n96:     /// quickly.\\n97:     ///\\n98:     /// # Panics\\n99:     ///\\n100:     /// Once a future has completed (returned `Ready` from `poll`), calling its\\n101:     /// `poll` method again may panic, block forever, or cause other kinds of\\n102:     /// problems; the `Future` trait places no requirements on the effects of\\n103:     /// such a call. However, as the `poll` method is not marked `unsafe`,\\n104:     /// Rust's usual rules apply: calls must never cause undefined behavior\\n105:     /// (memory corruption, incorrect use of `unsafe` functions, or the like),\\n106:     /// regardless of the future's state.\\n107:     ///\\n108:     /// [`Poll::Ready(val)`]: Poll::Ready\\n109:     /// [`Waker`]: crate::task::Waker\\n110:     /// [`Waker::wake`]: crate::task::Waker::wake\\n111:     #[lang = \\\"poll\\\"]\\n112:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n113:     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output>;\\n114: }\\n115: \\n116: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n117: impl<F: ?Sized + Future + Unpin> Future for &mut F {\\n118:     type Output = F::Output;\\n119: \\n120:     fn poll(mut self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\\n121:         F::poll(Pin::new(&mut **self), cx)\\n122:     }\\n123: }\\n124: \\n125: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n126: impl<P> Future for Pin<P>\\n127: where\\n128:     P: ops::DerefMut<Target: Future>,\\n129: {\\n130:     type Output = <<P as ops::Deref>::Target as Future>::Output;\\n131: \\n132:     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\\n133:         <P::Target as Future>::poll(self.as_deref_mut(), cx)\\n134:     }\\n135: }\\n136: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/library/core/src/future/future.rs\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: #![stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n2: \n3: use crate::ops;\n4: use crate::pin::Pin;\n5: use crate::task::{Context, Poll};\n6: \n7: /// A future represents an asynchronous computation, commonly obtained by use of\n8: /// [`async`].\n9: ///\n10: /// A future is a value that might not have finished computing yet. This kind of\n11: /// \"asynchronous value\" makes it possible for a thread to continue doing useful\n12: /// work while it waits for the value to become available.\n13: ///\n14: /// # The `poll` method\n15: ///\n16: /// The core method of future, `poll`, *attempts* to resolve the future into a\n17: /// final value. This method does not block if the value is not ready. Instead,\n18: /// the current task is scheduled to be woken up when it's possible to make\n19: /// further progress by `poll`ing again. The `context` passed to the `poll`\n20: /// method can provide a [`Waker`], which is a handle for waking up the current\n21: /// task.\n22: ///\n23: /// When using a future, you generally won't call `poll` directly, but instead\n24: /// `.await` the value.\n25: ///\n26: /// [`async`]: ../../std/keyword.async.html\n27: /// [`Waker`]: crate::task::Waker\n28: #[doc(notable_trait)]\n29: #[doc(search_unbox)]\n30: #[must_use = \"futures do nothing unless you `.await` or poll them\"]\n31: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n32: #[lang = \"future_trait\"]\n33: #[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(\n34:     label = \"`{Self}` is not a future\",\n35:     message = \"`{Self}` is not a future\"\n36: )]\n37: pub trait Future {\n38:     /// The type of value produced on completion.\n39:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n40:     #[lang = \"future_output\"]\n41:     type Output;\n42: \n43:     /// Attempts to resolve the future to a final value, registering\n44:     /// the current task for wakeup if the value is not yet available.\n45:     ///\n46:     /// # Return value\n47:     ///\n48:     /// This function returns:\n49:     ///\n50:     /// - [`Poll::Pending`] if the future is not ready yet\n51:     /// - [`Poll::Ready(val)`] with the result `val` of this future if it\n52:     ///   finished successfully.\n53:     ///\n54:     /// Once a future has finished, clients should not `poll` it again.\n55:     ///\n56:     /// When a future is not ready yet, `poll` returns `Poll::Pending` and\n57:     /// stores a clone of the [`Waker`] copied from the current [`Context`].\n58:     /// This [`Waker`] is then woken once the future can make progress.\n59:     /// For example, a future waiting for a socket to become\n60:     /// readable would call `.clone()` on the [`Waker`] and store it.\n61:     /// When a signal arrives elsewhere indicating that the socket is readable,\n62:     /// [`Waker::wake`] is called and the socket future's task is awoken.\n63:     /// Once a task has been woken up, it should attempt to `poll` the future\n64:     /// again, which may or may not produce a final value.\n65:     ///\n66:     /// Note that on multiple calls to `poll`, only the [`Waker`] from the\n67:     /// [`Context`] passed to the most recent call should be scheduled to\n68:     /// receive a wakeup.\n69:     ///\n70:     /// # Runtime characteristics\n71:     ///\n72:     /// Futures alone are *inert*; they must be *actively* `poll`ed for the\n73:     /// underlying computation to make progress, meaning that each time the\n74:     /// current task is woken up, it should actively re-`poll` pending futures\n75:     /// that it still has an interest in.\n76:     ///\n77:     /// Having said that, some Futures may represent a value that is being\n78:     /// computed in a different task. In this case, the future's underlying\n79:     /// computation is simply acting as a conduit for a value being computed\n80:     /// by that other task, which will proceed independently of the Future.\n81:     /// Futures of this kind are typically obtained when spawning a new task into an\n82:     /// async runtime.\n83:     ///\n84:     /// The `poll` function should not be called repeatedly in a tight loop --\n85:     /// instead, it should only be called when the future indicates that it is\n86:     /// ready to make progress (by calling `wake()`). If you're familiar with the\n87:     /// `poll(2)` or `select(2)` syscalls on Unix it's worth noting that futures\n88:     /// typically do *not* suffer the same problems of \"all wakeups must poll\n89:     /// all events\"; they are more like `epoll(4)`.\n90:     ///\n91:     /// An implementation of `poll` should strive to return quickly, and should\n92:     /// not block. Returning quickly prevents unnecessarily clogging up\n93:     /// threads or event loops. If it is known ahead of time that a call to\n94:     /// `poll` may end up taking a while, the work should be offloaded to a\n95:     /// thread pool (or something similar) to ensure that `poll` can return\n96:     /// quickly.\n97:     ///\n98:     /// # Panics\n99:     ///\n100:     /// Once a future has completed (returned `Ready` from `poll`), calling its\n101:     /// `poll` method again may panic, block forever, or cause other kinds of\n102:     /// problems; the `Future` trait places no requirements on the effects of\n103:     /// such a call. However, as the `poll` method is not marked `unsafe`,\n104:     /// Rust's usual rules apply: calls must never cause undefined behavior\n105:     /// (memory corruption, incorrect use of `unsafe` functions, or the like),\n106:     /// regardless of the future's state.\n107:     ///\n108:     /// [`Poll::Ready(val)`]: Poll::Ready\n109:     /// [`Waker`]: crate::task::Waker\n110:     /// [`Waker::wake`]: crate::task::Waker::wake\n111:     #[lang = \"poll\"]\n112:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n113:     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output>;\n114: }\n115: \n116: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n117: impl<F: ?Sized + Future + Unpin> Future for &mut F {\n118:     type Output = F::Output;\n119: \n120:     fn poll(mut self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\n121:         F::poll(Pin::new(&mut **self), cx)\n122:     }\n123: }\n124: \n125: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n126: impl<P> Future for Pin<P>\n127: where\n128:     P: ops::DerefMut<Target: Future>,\n129: {\n130:     type Output = <<P as ops::Deref>::Target as Future>::Output;\n131: \n132:     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\n133:         <P::Target as Future>::poll(self.as_deref_mut(), cx)\n134:     }\n135: }\n136: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/library/core/src/future/future.rs"}}}

Types and Traits for working with asynchronous tasks.\\n4: //!\\n5: //! **Note**: Some of the types in this module are only available\\n6: //! on platforms that support atomic loads and stores of pointers.\\n7: //! This may be detected at compile time using\\n8: //! `#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]`.\\n9: \\n10: use core::mem::ManuallyDrop;\\n11: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n12: use core::task::Waker;\\n13: use core::task::{LocalWaker, RawWaker, RawWakerVTable};\\n14: \\n15: use crate::rc::Rc;\\n16: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n17: use crate::sync::Arc;\\n18: \\n19: /// The implementation of waking a task on an executor.\\n20: ///\\n21: /// This trait can be used to create a [`Waker`]. An executor can define an\\n22: /// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\\n23: /// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\\n24: ///\\n25: /// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\\n26: /// [`RawWaker`]. It supports the common executor design in which the data used\\n27: /// to wake up a task is stored in an [`Arc`]. Some executors (especially\\n28: /// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\\n29: /// exists as an alternative for those systems.\\n30: ///\\n31: /// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\\n32: /// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\\n33: /// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\\n34: ///\\n35: /// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\\n36: ///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\\n37: ///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\\n38: ///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\\n39: ///\\n40: /// # Examples\\n41: ///\\n42: /// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\\n43: /// the current thread.\\n44: ///\\n45: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. In order to prevent\\n46: /// deadlocks, production-grade implementations will also need to handle\\n47: /// intermediate calls to `thread::unpark` as well as nested invocations.\\n48: ///\\n49: /// ```rust\\n50: /// use std::future::Future;\\n51: /// use std::sync::Arc;\\n52: /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Wake};\\n53: /// use std::thread::{self, Thread};\\n54: /// use core::pin::pin;\\n55: ///\\n56: /// /// A waker that wakes up the current thread when called.\\n57: /// struct ThreadWaker(Thread);\\n58: ///\\n59: /// impl Wake for ThreadWaker {\\n60: ///     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>) {\\n61: ///         self.0.unpark();\\n62: ///     }\\n63: /// }\\n64: ///\\n65: /// /// Run a future to completion on the current thread.\\n66: /// fn block_on<T>(fut: impl Future<Output = T>) -> T {\\n67: ///     // Pin the future so it can be polled.\\n68: ///     let mut fut = pin!(fut);\\n69: ///\\n70: ///     // Create a new context to be passed to the future.\\n71: ///     let t = thread::current();\\n72: ///     let waker = Arc::new(ThreadWaker(t)).into();\\n73: ///     let mut cx = Context::from_waker(&waker);\\n74: ///\\n75: ///     // Run the future to completion.\\n76: ///     loop {\\n77: ///         match fut.as_mut().poll(&mut cx) {\\n78: ///             Poll::Ready(res) => return res,\\n79: ///             Poll::Pending => thread::park(),\\n80: ///         }\\n81: ///     }\\n82: /// }\\n83: ///\\n84: /// block_on(async {\\n85: ///     println!(\\\"Hi from inside a future!\\\");\\n86: /// });\\n87: /// ```\\n88: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n89: #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n90: pub trait Wake {\\n91:     /// Wake this task.\\n92:     #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n93:     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>);\\n94: \\n95:     /// Wake this task without consuming the waker.\\n96:     ///\\n97:     /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\\n98:     /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\\n99:     /// [`Arc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\\n100:     ///\\n101:     /// [`wake`]: Wake::wake\\n102:     #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n103:     fn wake_by_ref(self: &Arc<Self>) {\\n104:         self.clone().wake();\\n105:     }\\n106: }\\n107: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n108: #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n109: impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for Waker {\\n110:     /// Use a [`Wake`]-able type as a `Waker`.\\n111:     ///\\n112:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\\n113:     fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> Waker {\\n114:         // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\\n115:         // a RawWaker from Arc<W>.\\n116:         unsafe { Waker::from_raw(raw_waker(waker)) }\\n117:     }\\n118: }\\n119: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n120: #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n121: impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker {\\n122:     /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\\n123:     ///\\n124:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\\n125:     fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\\n126:         raw_waker(waker)\\n127:     }\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: // NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\\n131: // inlining this into the `From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\\n132: // the safety of `From<Arc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\\n133: // trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\\n134: // explicitly.\\n135: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n136: #[inline(always)]\\n137: fn raw_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\\n138:     // Increment the reference count of the arc to clone it.\\n139:     //\\n140:     // The #[inline(always)] is to ensure that raw_waker and clone_waker are\\n141:     // always generated in the same code generation unit as one another, and\\n142:     // therefore that the structurally identical const-promoted RawWakerVTable\\n143:     // within both functions is deduplicated at LLVM IR code generation time.\\n144:     // This allows optimizing Waker::will_wake to a single pointer comparison of\\n145:     // the vtable pointers, rather than comparing all four function pointers\\n146:     // within the vtables.\\n147:     #[inline(always)]\\n148:     unsafe fn clone_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\\n149:         unsafe { Arc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\\n150:         RawWaker::new(\\n151:             waker,\\n152:             &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\\n153:         )\\n154:     }\\n155: \\n156:     // Wake by value, moving the Arc into the Wake::wake function\\n157:     unsafe fn wake<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n158:         let waker = unsafe { Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\\n159:         <W as Wake>::wake(waker);\\n160:     }\\n161: \\n162:     // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\\n163:     unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n164:         let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\\n165:         <W as Wake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\\n166:     }\\n167: \\n168:     // Decrement the reference count of the Arc on drop\\n169:     unsafe fn drop_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n170:         unsafe { Arc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\\n171:     }\\n172: \\n173:     RawWaker::new(\\n174:         Arc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\\n175:         &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\\n176:     )\\n177: }\\n178: \\n179: /// An analogous trait to `Wake` but used to construct a `LocalWaker`.\\n180: ///\\n181: /// This API works in exactly the same way as `Wake`,\\n182: /// except that it uses an `Rc` instead of an `Arc`,\\n183: /// and the result is a `LocalWaker` instead of a `Waker`.\\n184: ///\\n185: /// The benefits of using `LocalWaker` over `Waker` are that it allows the local waker\\n186: /// to hold data that does not implement `Send` and `Sync`. Additionally, it saves calls\\n187: /// to `Arc::clone`, which requires atomic synchronization.\\n188: ///\\n189: ///\\n190: /// # Examples\\n191: ///\\n192: /// This is a simplified example of a `spawn` and a `block_on` function. The `spawn` function\\n193: /// is used to push new tasks onto the run queue, while the block on function will remove them\\n194: /// and poll them. When a task is woken, it will put itself back on the run queue to be polled\\n195: /// by the executor.\\n196: ///\\n197: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. A real world example would interleave\\n198: /// poll calls with calls to an io reactor to wait for events instead of spinning on a loop.\\n199: ///\\n200: /// ```rust\\n201: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\\n202: /// use std::task::{LocalWake, ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker};\\n203: /// use std::future::Future;\\n204: /// use std::pin::Pin;\\n205: /// use std::rc::Rc;\\n206: /// use std::cell::RefCell;\\n207: /// use std::collections::VecDeque;\\n208: ///\\n209: ///\\n210: /// thread_local! {\\n211: ///     // A queue containing all tasks ready to do progress\\n212: ///     static RUN_QUEUE: RefCell<VecDeque<Rc<Task>>> = RefCell::default();\\n213: /// }\\n214: ///\\n215: /// type BoxedFuture = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = ()>>>;\\n216: ///\\n217: /// struct Task(RefCell<BoxedFuture>);\\n218: ///\\n219: /// impl LocalWake for Task {\\n220: ///     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>) {\\n221: ///         RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\\n222: ///             queue.push_back(self)\\n223: ///         })\\n224: ///     }\\n225: /// }\\n226: ///\\n227: /// fn spawn<F>(future: F)\\n228: /// where\\n229: ///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Send + Sync\\n230: /// {\\n231: ///     let task = RefCell::new(Box::pin(future));\\n232: ///     RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\\n233: ///         queue.push_back(Rc::new(Task(task)));\\n234: ///     });\\n235: /// }\\n236: ///\\n237: /// fn block_on<F>(future: F)\\n238: /// where\\n239: ///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Sync + Send\\n240: /// {\\n241: ///     spawn(future);\\n242: ///     loop {\\n243: ///         let Some(task) = RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| queue.pop_front()) else {\\n244: ///             // we exit, since there are no more tasks remaining on the queue\\n245: ///             return;\\n246: ///         };\\n247: ///\\n248: ///         // cast the Rc<Task> into a `LocalWaker`\\n249: ///         let local_waker: LocalWaker = task.clone().into();\\n250: ///         // Build the context using `ContextBuilder`\\n251: ///         let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\\n252: ///             .local_waker(&local_waker)\\n253: ///             .build();\\n254: ///\\n255: ///         // Poll the task\\n256: ///         let _ = task.0\\n257: ///             .borrow_mut()\\n258: ///             .as_mut()\\n259: ///             .poll(&mut cx);\\n260: ///     }\\n261: /// }\\n262: ///\\n263: /// block_on(async {\\n264: ///     println!(\\\"hello world\\\");\\n265: /// });\\n266: /// ```\\n267: ///\\n268: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n269: pub trait LocalWake {\\n270:     /// Wake this task.\\n271:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n272:     fn Types and Traits for working with asynchronous tasks.\\n4: //!\\n5: //! **Note**: Some of the types in this module are only available\\n6: //! on platforms that support atomic loads and stores of pointers.\\n7: //! This may be detected at compile time using\\n8: //! `#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]`.\\n9: \\n10: use core::mem::ManuallyDrop;\\n11: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n12: use core::task::Waker;\\n13: use core::task::{LocalWaker, RawWaker, RawWakerVTable};\\n14: \\n15: use crate::rc::Rc;\\n16: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n17: use crate::sync::Arc;\\n18: \\n19: /// The implementation of waking a task on an executor.\\n20: ///\\n21: /// This trait can be used to create a [`Waker`]. An executor can define an\\n22: /// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\\n23: /// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\\n24: ///\\n25: /// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\\n26: /// [`RawWaker`]. It supports the common executor design in which the data used\\n27: /// to wake up a task is stored in an [`Arc`]. Some executors (especially\\n28: /// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\\n29: /// exists as an alternative for those systems.\\n30: ///\\n31: /// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\\n32: /// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\\n33: /// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\\n34: ///\\n35: /// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\\n36: ///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\\n37: ///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\\n38: ///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\\n39: ///\\n40: /// # Examples\\n41: ///\\n42: /// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\\n43: /// the current thread.\\n44: ///\\n45: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. In order to prevent\\n46: /// deadlocks, production-grade implementations will also need to handle\\n47: /// intermediate calls to `thread::unpark` as well as nested invocations.\\n48: ///\\n49: /// ```rust\\n50: /// use std::future::Future;\\n51: /// use std::sync::Arc;\\n52: /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Wake};\\n53: /// use std::thread::{self, Thread};\\n54: /// use core::pin::pin;\\n55: ///\\n56: /// /// A waker that wakes up the current thread when called.\\n57: /// struct ThreadWaker(Thread);\\n58: ///\\n59: /// impl Wake for ThreadWaker {\\n60: ///     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>) {\\n61: ///         self.0.unpark();\\n62: ///     }\\n63: /// }\\n64: ///\\n65: /// /// Run a future to completion on the current thread.\\n66: /// fn block_on<T>(fut: impl Future<Output = T>) -> T {\\n67: ///     // Pin the future so it can be polled.\\n68: ///     let mut fut = pin!(fut);\\n69: ///\\n70: ///     // Create a new context to be passed to the future.\\n71: ///     let t = thread::current();\\n72: ///     let waker = Arc::new(ThreadWaker(t)).into();\\n73: ///     let mut cx = Context::from_waker(&waker);\\n74: ///\\n75: ///     // Run the future to completion.\\n76: ///     loop {\\n77: ///         match fut.as_mut().poll(&mut cx) {\\n78: ///             Poll::Ready(res) => return res,\\n79: ///             Poll::Pending => thread::park(),\\n80: ///         }\\n81: ///     }\\n82: /// }\\n83: ///\\n84: /// block_on(async {\\n85: ///     println!(\\\"Hi from inside a future!\\\");\\n86: /// });\\n87: /// ```\\n88: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n89: #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n90: pub trait Wake {\\n91:     /// Wake this task.\\n92:     #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n93:     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>);\\n94: \\n95:     /// Wake this task without consuming the waker.\\n96:     ///\\n97:     /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\\n98:     /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\\n99:     /// [`Arc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\\n100:     ///\\n101:     /// [`wake`]: Wake::wake\\n102:     #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n103:     fn wake_by_ref(self: &Arc<Self>) {\\n104:         self.clone().wake();\\n105:     }\\n106: }\\n107: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n108: #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n109: impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for Waker {\\n110:     /// Use a [`Wake`]-able type as a `Waker`.\\n111:     ///\\n112:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\\n113:     fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> Waker {\\n114:         // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\\n115:         // a RawWaker from Arc<W>.\\n116:         unsafe { Waker::from_raw(raw_waker(waker)) }\\n117:     }\\n118: }\\n119: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n120: #[stable(feature = \\\"wake_trait\\\", since = \\\"1.51.0\\\")]\\n121: impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker {\\n122:     /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\\n123:     ///\\n124:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\\n125:     fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\\n126:         raw_waker(waker)\\n127:     }\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: // NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\\n131: // inlining this into the `From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\\n132: // the safety of `From<Arc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\\n133: // trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\\n134: // explicitly.\\n135: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \\\"ptr\\\")]\\n136: #[inline(always)]\\n137: fn raw_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\\n138:     // Increment the reference count of the arc to clone it.\\n139:     //\\n140:     // The #[inline(always)] is to ensure that raw_waker and clone_waker are\\n141:     // always generated in the same code generation unit as one another, and\\n142:     // therefore that the structurally identical const-promoted RawWakerVTable\\n143:     // within both functions is deduplicated at LLVM IR code generation time.\\n144:     // This allows optimizing Waker::will_wake to a single pointer comparison of\\n145:     // the vtable pointers, rather than comparing all four function pointers\\n146:     // within the vtables.\\n147:     #[inline(always)]\\n148:     unsafe fn clone_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\\n149:         unsafe { Arc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\\n150:         RawWaker::new(\\n151:             waker,\\n152:             &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\\n153:         )\\n154:     }\\n155: \\n156:     // Wake by value, moving the Arc into the Wake::wake function\\n157:     unsafe fn wake<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n158:         let waker = unsafe { Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\\n159:         <W as Wake>::wake(waker);\\n160:     }\\n161: \\n162:     // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\\n163:     unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n164:         let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\\n165:         <W as Wake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\\n166:     }\\n167: \\n168:     // Decrement the reference count of the Arc on drop\\n169:     unsafe fn drop_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n170:         unsafe { Arc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\\n171:     }\\n172: \\n173:     RawWaker::new(\\n174:         Arc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\\n175:         &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\\n176:     )\\n177: }\\n178: \\n179: /// An analogous trait to `Wake` but used to construct a `LocalWaker`.\\n180: ///\\n181: /// This API works in exactly the same way as `Wake`,\\n182: /// except that it uses an `Rc` instead of an `Arc`,\\n183: /// and the result is a `LocalWaker` instead of a `Waker`.\\n184: ///\\n185: /// The benefits of using `LocalWaker` over `Waker` are that it allows the local waker\\n186: /// to hold data that does not implement `Send` and `Sync`. Additionally, it saves calls\\n187: /// to `Arc::clone`, which requires atomic synchronization.\\n188: ///\\n189: ///\\n190: /// # Examples\\n191: ///\\n192: /// This is a simplified example of a `spawn` and a `block_on` function. The `spawn` function\\n193: /// is used to push new tasks onto the run queue, while the block on function will remove them\\n194: /// and poll them. When a task is woken, it will put itself back on the run queue to be polled\\n195: /// by the executor.\\n196: ///\\n197: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. A real world example would interleave\\n198: /// poll calls with calls to an io reactor to wait for events instead of spinning on a loop.\\n199: ///\\n200: /// ```rust\\n201: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\\n202: /// use std::task::{LocalWake, ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker};\\n203: /// use std::future::Future;\\n204: /// use std::pin::Pin;\\n205: /// use std::rc::Rc;\\n206: /// use std::cell::RefCell;\\n207: /// use std::collections::VecDeque;\\n208: ///\\n209: ///\\n210: /// thread_local! {\\n211: ///     // A queue containing all tasks ready to do progress\\n212: ///     static RUN_QUEUE: RefCell<VecDeque<Rc<Task>>> = RefCell::default();\\n213: /// }\\n214: ///\\n215: /// type BoxedFuture = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = ()>>>;\\n216: ///\\n217: /// struct Task(RefCell<BoxedFuture>);\\n218: ///\\n219: /// impl LocalWake for Task {\\n220: ///     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>) {\\n221: ///         RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\\n222: ///             queue.push_back(self)\\n223: ///         })\\n224: ///     }\\n225: /// }\\n226: ///\\n227: /// fn spawn<F>(future: F)\\n228: /// where\\n229: ///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Send + Sync\\n230: /// {\\n231: ///     let task = RefCell::new(Box::pin(future));\\n232: ///     RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\\n233: ///         queue.push_back(Rc::new(Task(task)));\\n234: ///     });\\n235: /// }\\n236: ///\\n237: /// fn block_on<F>(future: F)\\n238: /// where\\n239: ///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Sync + Send\\n240: /// {\\n241: ///     spawn(future);\\n242: ///     loop {\\n243: ///         let Some(task) = RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| queue.pop_front()) else {\\n244: ///             // we exit, since there are no more tasks remaining on the queue\\n245: ///             return;\\n246: ///         };\\n247: ///\\n248: ///         // cast the Rc<Task> into a `LocalWaker`\\n249: ///         let local_waker: LocalWaker = task.clone().into();\\n250: ///         // Build the context using `ContextBuilder`\\n251: ///         let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\\n252: ///             .local_waker(&local_waker)\\n253: ///             .build();\\n254: ///\\n255: ///         // Poll the task\\n256: ///         let _ = task.0\\n257: ///             .borrow_mut()\\n258: ///             .as_mut()\\n259: ///             .poll(&mut cx);\\n260: ///     }\\n261: /// }\\n262: ///\\n263: /// block_on(async {\\n264: ///     println!(\\\"hello world\\\");\\n265: /// });\\n266: /// ```\\n267: ///\\n268: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n269: pub trait LocalWake {\\n270:     /// Wake this task.\\n271:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n272:     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>);\\n273: \\n274:     /// Wake this task without consuming the local waker.\\n275:     ///\\n276:     /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\\n277:     /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\\n278:     /// [`Rc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\\n279:     ///\\n280:     /// [`wake`]: LocalWaker::wake\\n281:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n282:     fn wake_by_ref(self: &Rc<Self>) {\\n283:         self.clone().wake();\\n284:     }\\n285: }\\n286: \\n287: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n288: impl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for LocalWaker {\\n289:     /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `LocalWaker`.\\n290:     ///\\n291:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\\n292:     fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> LocalWaker {\\n293:         // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\\n294:         // a RawWaker from Rc<W>.\\n295:         unsafe { LocalWaker::from_raw(local_raw_waker(waker)) }\\n296:     }\\n297: }\\n298: #[allow(ineffective_unstable_trait_impl)]\\n299: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n300: impl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker {\\n301:     /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\\n302:     ///\\n303:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\\n304:     fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\\n305:         local_raw_waker(waker)\\n306:     }\\n307: }\\n308: \\n309: // NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\\n310: // inlining this into the `From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\\n311: // the safety of `From<Rc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\\n312: // trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\\n313: // explicitly.\\n314: #[inline(always)]\\n315: fn local_raw_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\\n316:     // Increment the reference count of the Rc to clone it.\\n317:     //\\n318:     // Refer to the comment on raw_waker's clone_waker regarding why this is\\n319:     // always inline.\\n320:     #[inline(always)]\\n321:     unsafe fn clone_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\\n322:         unsafe { Rc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\\n323:         RawWaker::new(\\n324:             waker,\\n325:             &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\\n326:         )\\n327:     }\\n328: \\n329:     // Wake by value, moving the Rc into the LocalWake::wake function\\n330:     unsafe fn wake<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n331:         let waker = unsafe { Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\\n332:         <W as LocalWake>::wake(waker);\\n333:     }\\n334: \\n335:     // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\\n336:     unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n337:         let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\\n338:         <W as LocalWake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\\n339:     }\\n340: \\n341:     // Decrement the reference count of the Rc on drop\\n342:     unsafe fn drop_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\\n343:         unsafe { Rc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\\n344:     }\\n345: \\n346:     RawWaker::new(\\n347:         Rc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\\n348:         &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\\n349:     )\\n350: }\\n351: #![stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n2: \n3: //! Types and Traits for working with asynchronous tasks.\n4: //!\n5: //! **Note**: Some of the types in this module are only available\n6: //! on platforms that support atomic loads and stores of pointers.\n7: //! This may be detected at compile time using\n8: //! `#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]`.\n9: \n10: use core::mem::ManuallyDrop;\n11: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n12: use core::task::Waker;\n13: use core::task::{LocalWaker, RawWaker, RawWakerVTable};\n14: \n15: use crate::rc::Rc;\n16: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n17: use crate::sync::Arc;\n18: \n19: /// The implementation of waking a task on an executor.\n20: ///\n21: /// This trait can be used to create a [`Waker`]. An executor can define an\n22: /// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\n23: /// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\n24: ///\n25: /// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\n26: /// [`RawWaker`]. It supports the common executor design in which the data used\n27: /// to wake up a task is stored in an [`Arc`]. Some executors (especially\n28: /// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\n29: /// exists as an alternative for those systems.\n30: ///\n31: /// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\n32: /// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\n33: /// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\n34: ///\n35: /// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\n36: ///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\n37: ///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\n38: ///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\n39: ///\n40: /// # Examples\n41: ///\n42: /// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\n43: /// the current thread.\n44: ///\n45: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. In order to prevent\n46: /// deadlocks, production-grade implementations will also need to handle\n47: /// intermediate calls to `thread::unpark` as well as nested invocations.\n48: ///\n49: /// ```rust\n50: /// use std::future::Future;\n51: /// use std::sync::Arc;\n52: /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Wake};\n53: /// use std::thread::{self, Thread};\n54: /// use core::pin::pin;\n55: ///\n56: /// /// A waker that wakes up the current thread when called.\n57: /// struct ThreadWaker(Thread);\n58: ///\n59: /// impl Wake for ThreadWaker {\n60: ///     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>) {\n61: ///         self.0.unpark();\n62: ///     }\n63: /// }\n64: ///\n65: /// /// Run a future to completion on the current thread.\n66: /// fn block_on<T>(fut: impl Future<Output = T>) -> T {\n67: ///     // Pin the future so it can be polled.\n68: ///     let mut fut = pin!(fut);\n69: ///\n70: ///     // Create a new context to be passed to the future.\n71: ///     let t = thread::current();\n72: ///     let waker = Arc::new(ThreadWaker(t)).into();\n73: ///     let mut cx = Context::from_waker(&waker);\n74: ///\n75: ///     // Run the future to completion.\n76: ///     loop {\n77: ///         match fut.as_mut().poll(&mut cx) {\n78: ///             Poll::Ready(res) => return res,\n79: ///             Poll::Pending => thread::park(),\n80: ///         }\n81: ///     }\n82: /// }\n83: ///\n84: /// block_on(async {\n85: ///     println!(\"Hi from inside a future!\");\n86: /// });\n87: /// ```\n88: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n89: #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n90: pub trait Wake {\n91:     /// Wake this task.\n92:     #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n93:     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>);\n94: \n95:     /// Wake this task without consuming the waker.\n96:     ///\n97:     /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\n98:     /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\n99:     /// [`Arc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n100:     ///\n101:     /// [`wake`]: Wake::wake\n102:     #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n103:     fn wake_by_ref(self: &Arc<Self>) {\n104:         self.clone().wake();\n105:     }\n106: }\n107: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n108: #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n109: impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for Waker {\n110:     /// Use a [`Wake`]-able type as a `Waker`.\n111:     ///\n112:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n113:     fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> Waker {\n114:         // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\n115:         // a RawWaker from impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker {\n122:     /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n123:     ///\n124:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n125:     fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n126:         raw_waker(waker)\n127:     }\n128: }\n129: \n130: // NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n131: // inlining this into the `From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n132: // the safety of `From<Arc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n133: // trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n134: // explicitly.\n135: #[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n136: #[inline(always)]\n137: fn raw_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n138:     // Increment the reference count of the arc to clone it.\n139:     //\n140:     // The #[inline(always)] is to ensure that raw_waker and clone_waker are\n141:     // always generated in the same code generation unit as one another, and\n142:     // therefore that the structurally identical const-promoted RawWakerVTable\n143:     // within both functions is Arc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n150:         RawWaker::new(\n151:             waker,\n152:             &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n153:         )\n154:     }\n155: \n156:     // Wake by value, moving the Arc into the Wake::wake function\n157:     unsafe fn wake<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n158:         let waker = unsafe { Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n159:         <W as Wake>::wake(waker);\n160:     }\n161: \n162:     // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n163:     unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n164:         let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n165:         <W as Wake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n166:     }\n167: \n168:     // Decrement the reference count of the Arc on drop\n169:     unsafe fn drop_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n170:         unsafe { Arc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n171:     }\n172: \n173:     RawWaker::new(\n174:         Arc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n175:         &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n176:     )\n177: }\n178: \n179: /// An analogous trait to `Wake` but used to construct a `LocalWaker`.\n180: ///\n181: /// This API works in exactly the same way as `Wake`,\n182: /// except that it uses an `Rc` instead of an `Arc`,\n183: /// and the result is a `LocalWaker` instead of a `Waker`.\n184: ///\n185: /// The benefits of using `LocalWaker` over `Waker` are that it allows the local waker\n186: /// to hold data that does not implement `Send` and `Sync`. Additionally, it saves calls\n187: /// to `Arc::clone`, which requires atomic synchronization.\n188: ///\n189: ///\n190: /// # Examples\n191: ///\n192: /// This is a simplified example of a `spawn` and a `block_on` function. The `spawn` function\n193: /// is used to push new tasks onto the run queue, while the block on function will remove them\n194: /// and poll them. When a task is woken, it will put itself back on the run queue to be polled\n195: /// by the executor.\n196: ///\n197: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. A real world example would interleave\n198: /// poll calls with calls to an io reactor to wait for events instead of spinning on a loop.\n199: ///\n200: /// ```rust\n201: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\n202: /// use std::task::{LocalWake, ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker};\n203: /// use std::future::Future;\n204: /// use std::pin::Pin;\n205: /// use std::rc::Rc;\n206: /// use std::cell::RefCell;\n207: /// use std::collections::VecDeque;\n208: ///\n209: ///\n210: /// thread_local! {\n211: ///     // A queue containing all tasks ready to do progress\n212: ///     static RUN_QUEUE: RefCell<VecDeque<Rc<Task>>> = RefCell::default();\n213: /// }\n214: ///\n215: /// type BoxedFuture = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = ()>>>;\n216: ///\n217: /// struct Task(RefCell<BoxedFuture>);\n218: ///\n219: /// impl LocalWake for Task {\n220: ///     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>) {\n221: ///         RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n222: ///             queue.push_back(self)\n223: ///         })\n224: ///     }\n225: /// }\n226: ///\n227: /// fn spawn<F>(future: F)\n228: /// where\n229: ///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Send + Sync\n230: /// {\n231: ///     let task = RefCell::new(Box::pin(future));\n232: ///     RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n233: ///         queue.push_back(Rc::new(Task(task)));\n234: ///     });\n235: /// }\n236: ///\n237: /// fn block_on<F>(future: F)\n238: /// where\n239: ///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Sync + Send\n240: /// {\n241: ///     spawn(future);\n242: ///     loop {\n243: ///         let Some(task) = RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| queue.pop_front()) else {\n244: ///             // we exit, since there are no more tasks remaining on the queue\n245: ///             return;\n246: ///         };\n247: ///\n248: ///         // cast the Rc<Task> into a `LocalWaker`\n249: ///         let local_waker: LocalWaker = task.clone().into();\n250: ///         // Build the context using `ContextBuilder`\n251: ///         let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\n252: ///             .local_waker(&local_waker)\n253: ///             .build();\n254: ///\n255: ///         // Poll the task\n256: ///         let _ = task.0\n257: ///             .borrow_mut()\n258: ///             .as_mut()\n259: ///             .poll(&mut cx);\n260: ///     }\n261: /// }\n262: ///\n263: /// block_on(async {\n264: ///     println!(\"hello world\");\n265: /// });\n266: /// ```\n267: ///\n268: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n269: pub trait LocalWake {\n270:     /// Wake this task.\n271:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n272:     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>);\n273: \n274:     /// Wake this task without consuming the local waker.\n275:     ///\n276:     /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\n277:     /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\n278:     /// [`Rc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n279:     ///\n280:     /// [`wake`]: LocalWaker::wake\n281:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n282:     fn wake_by_ref(self: &Rc<Self>) {\n283:         self.clone().wake();\n284:     }\n285: }\n286: \n287: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n288: impl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for LocalWaker {\n289:     /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `LocalWaker`.\n290:     ///\n291:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n292:     fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> LocalWaker {\n293:         // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\n294:         // a RawWaker from Rc<W>.\n295:         unsafe { LocalWaker::from_raw(local_raw_waker(waker)) }\n296:     }\n297: }\n298: #[allow(ineffective_unstable_trait_impl)]\n299: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n300: impl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker {\n301:     /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n302:     ///\n303:     /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n304:     fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n305:         local_raw_waker(waker)\n306:     }\n307: }\n308: \n309: // NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n310: // inlining this into the `From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n311: // the safety of `From<Rc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n312: // trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n313: // explicitly.\n314: #[inline(always)]\n315: fn local_raw_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n316:     // Increment the reference count of the Rc to clone it.\n317:     //\n318:     // Refer to the comment on raw_waker's clone_waker regarding why this is\n319:     // always inline.\n320:     #[inline(always)]\n321:     unsafe fn clone_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\n322:         unsafe { Rc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n323:         RawWaker::new(\n324:             waker,\n325:             &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n326:         )\n327:     }\n328: \n329:     // Wake by value, moving the Rc into the LocalWake::wake function\n330:     unsafe fn wake<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n331:         let waker = unsafe { Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n332:         <W as LocalWake>::wake(waker);\n333:     }\n334: \n335:     // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n336:     unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n337:         let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n338:         <W as LocalWake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n339:     }\n340: \n341:     // Decrement the reference count of the Rc on drop\n342:     unsafe fn drop_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n343:         unsafe { Rc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n344:     }\n345: \n346:     RawWaker::new(\n347:         Rc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n348:         &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n349:     )\n350: }\n351: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/library/alloc/src/task.rs"}}}

mechanism across multiple files in the `core` and `alloc` libraries:\\n\\n**Core Waker Mechanism (library/core/src/task/wake.rs):**\\nThe foundational types are defined here. `RawWaker` (lines 22-31) is a low-level waker consisting of a data pointer and a static reference to a `RawWakerVTable`. The `RawWakerVTable` struct (lines 109-140) is a vtable containing four function pointers: `clone`, `wake`, `wake_by_ref`, and `drop`. These functions are called by the executor to manage wakeup behavior.\\n\\nThe `Waker` struct (lines 407-409) wraps a `RawWaker` and provides safe, Send+Sync methods for waking tasks. It implements `Clone` (lines 612-665), where cloning delegates to the vtable's `clone` function. The `LocalWaker` struct (lines 740-742) is analogous to `Waker` but does not implement Send or Sync, allowing it to hold non-thread-safe data.\\n\\nThe `Context` struct (lines 218-230) is passed to futures during polling and provides access to the waker. It can be constructed via `ContextBuilder` (lines 301-313), which allows setting both a regular `Waker` and a `LocalWaker`.\\n\\n**Future Polling Mechanism (library/core/src/future/future.rs):**\\nThe `Future` trait (lines 37-114) defines the core polling interface with a `poll` method (line 113) that takes a mutable reference to `Context` and returns `Poll<Self::Output>`. When a future is not ready, it stores a clone of the waker from the context and calls it later to signal readiness.\\n\\n**Poll Enum (library/core/src/task/poll.rs):**\\nThe `Poll` enum (lines 14-28) indicates whether a future is `Ready` with a value or `Pending`, awaiting wakeup.\\n\\n**High-Level Wake Traits (library/alloc/src/task.rs):**\\nFor ergonomics, the `Wake` trait (lines 90-106) allows executors to implement waking via an Arc-based approach. The `raw_waker` function (lines 137-177) converts Arc<W> into a `RawWaker` by creating vtable entries that manage Arc reference counting. Similarly, `LocalWake` trait (lines 269-285) and `local_raw_waker` function (lines 315-350) provide the same functionality for Rc-based local wakers.\\n\\n**The Polling Loop:**\\nThe fundamental async pattern is: (1) An executor calls `Future::poll()` with a context containing a waker, (2) if the future returns `Poll::Pending`, it clones and stores the waker, (3) when the future is ready to make progress, it calls `Waker::wake()` or `Waker::wake_by_ref()`, which invokes the vtable's wake function, (4) the executor then calls `poll()` again on the task.\\n\\nThis design separates the high-level `Wake` trait (for convenience in alloc) from the low-level `RawWaker` mechanism (for bare-metal and embedded systems), allowing flexible executor implementations while maintaining consistent semantics.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5664,"cache_read_input_tokens":73216,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5664},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1019be55-e39f-4a7a-8b30-264da596c856","uuid":"088ee318-ae20-4782-b028-08120a4a813e"}

mechanism across multiple files in the `core` and `alloc` libraries:\\n\\n**Core Waker Mechanism (library/core/src/task/wake.rs):**\\nThe foundational types are defined here. `RawWaker` (lines 22-31) is a low-level waker consisting of a data pointer and a static reference to a `RawWakerVTable`. The `RawWakerVTable` struct (lines 109-140) is a vtable containing four function pointers: `clone`, `wake`, `wake_by_ref`, and `drop`. These functions are called by the executor to manage wakeup behavior.\\n\\nThe `Waker` struct (lines 407-409) wraps a `RawWaker` and provides safe, Send+Sync methods for waking tasks. It implements `Clone` (lines 612-665), where cloning delegates to the vtable's `clone` function. The `LocalWaker` struct (lines 740-742) is analogous to `Waker` but does not implement Send or Sync, allowing it to hold non-thread-safe data.\\n\\nThe `Context` struct (lines 218-230) is passed to futures during polling and provides access to the waker. It can be constructed via `ContextBuilder` (lines 301-313), which allows setting both a regular `Waker` and a `LocalWaker`.\\n\\n**Future Polling Mechanism (library/core/src/future/future.rs):**\\nThe `Future` trait (lines 37-114) defines the core polling interface with a `poll` method (line 113) that takes a mutable reference to `Context` and returns `Poll<Self::Output>`. When a future is not ready, it stores a clone of the waker from the context and calls it later to signal readiness.\\n\\n**Poll Enum (library/core/src/task/poll.rs):**\\nThe `Poll` enum (lines 14-28) indicates whether a future is `Ready` with a value or `Pending`, awaiting wakeup.\\n\\n**High-Level Wake Traits (library/alloc/src/task.rs):**\\nFor ergonomics, the `Wake` trait (lines 90-106) allows executors to implement waking via an Arc-based approach. The `raw_waker` function (lines 137-177) converts Arc<W> into a `RawWaker` by creating vtable entries that manage Arc reference counting. Similarly, `LocalWake` trait (lines 269-285) and `local_raw_waker` function (lines 315-350) provide the same functionality for Rc-based local wakers.\\n\\n**The Polling Loop:**\\nThe fundamental async pattern is: (1) An executor calls `Future::poll()` with a context containing a waker, (2) if the future returns `Poll::Pending`, it clones and stores the waker, (3) when the future is ready to make progress, it calls `Waker::wake()` or `Waker::wake_by_ref()`, which invokes the vtable's wake function, (4) the executor then calls `poll()` again on the task.\\n\\nThis design separates the high-level `Wake` trait (for convenience in alloc) from the low-level `RawWaker` mechanism (for bare-metal and embedded systems), allowing flexible executor implementations while maintaining consistent semantics.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
